# Consultation 69 — Phase 4.1 DX polish, post-application review

Consultation 68 returned dual-GREEN with two specific pushbacks:
- **#1 stricter**: bundleHash must be exactly 64 hex (SHA-256, 32
  bytes), signature exactly 128 hex (Ed25519, 64 bytes). Not "64
  or 128" — strictly 64 for the hash, 128 for the signature.
- **#4 not deferred wholesale**: `sdk-plugin/examples/minimal/`
  already exists; Phase 4.1 should make it discoverable + replace
  the `"00"` placeholders.

All Phase 4.1 items have been applied. This is the post-application
review pass.

## Phase 4.1 changes applied

### #1 — Manifest validator + placeholder cleanup
- `sdk-plugin/src/manifest.ts:126-150`: validator now rejects
  `bundleHash` that isn't exactly 64 lowercase hex chars and
  `signature` that isn't exactly 128 hex chars. Error messages
  reference `sign-bundle.ts` so authors know where to look.
- `sdk-plugin/examples/minimal/src/plugin.ts`,
  `sdk-plugin/examples/minimal/manifest.json`: replaced `"00"`
  placeholders with `UNSIGNED-PLACEHOLDER-REPLACE-WITH-SIGN-BUNDLE`
  — loud failure mode that's unambiguous when an author forgets
  to sign. Inline comments in `plugin.ts` explain the build →
  sign → publish cycle and why the placeholders are deliberately
  invalid.
- `sdk-plugin/README.md`: rewrote the §"Minimal Plugin" section
  to walk through build → sign → publish with the actual command
  invocations. Pointer to the new minimal example.
- `sdk-plugin/test/{manifest,base-plugin,network}.test.ts`:
  updated to use `'a'.repeat(64)` / `'b'.repeat(128)` for hash and
  signature respectively. New tests in `manifest.test.ts` assert
  the length checks and the UNSIGNED placeholder rejection.
- SDK tests: 29/29 passing.

### #4 — Surface the existing minimal example
- `sdk-plugin/examples/minimal/README.md` (NEW): documents what
  this example is, what files it ships, how to build → sign →
  publish, and what it does NOT do (no backend round-trip yet —
  that's V1.5 #7).
- `examples/README.md` (NEW): top-level index pointing to
  `trading-bot/` (sender side) and `sdk-plugin/examples/minimal/`
  (plugin side). Notes that a combined round-trip example is
  tracked under V1.5 DX (item #7 in ROADMAP).

### #2 — Pairing wording cleanup
- `sdk-python/README.md`: removed the "M7 wires this; for now in
  dev, use client.set_pairing(...)" TODO-style language. The new
  Quickstart shows the V1 manual flow (user copies `user_id` +
  `pairing_key_hex` off the device confirmation screen, types
  them into the sender's backend) as the **canonical** V1 path,
  with a forward-pointer to the V1.5 DX roadmap item for the
  automated bootstrap exchange.

### #3 — Wildcard glob grammar documented
- `docs/integration-guide.md` §3.1 (NEW): documents that `*`
  matches exactly one host or path segment, never multiple, with
  the boundary rule (`[^./]*` in host, `[^/]*` in path) and
  examples of common mistakes (`/api/*` not matching `/api/v1/users`,
  `*.example.com` not matching `a.b.example.com`). Notes that the
  same matcher gates template action endpoints at publish time.
- This is the rule implemented by `sdk-plugin/src/network.ts:48-69`
  and `android/.../EndpointMatcher.kt`; the doc surfaces it.

### #5 — `platform.network.fetch` contract documented
- `docs/integration-guide.md` §3.2 (NEW): full contract — returns
  `Response` for any HTTP status; throws on `endpoint_not_declared`
  / `cleartext_in_release` / network failures; OkHttp default
  timeouts; cookies disabled at the bridge; no streaming bodies;
  no `AbortController`. Example code block showing success +
  failure handling.

### #6 — ROADMAP V1.5 Developer Experience section
- `docs/ROADMAP.md`: new V1.5 — Developer experience subsection
  with four items: automated pairing handshake (#6), full
  round-trip example plugin (#7), `npm create @syncler/plugin`
  scaffold (#8), validator polish backlog (#9). Renumbered V2/V3/V4
  items so the list is monotonic.

### Structural — §9 split
- `docs/integration-guide.md`: §9 renamed to "Common server
  errors" (only items the server returned 4xx/5xx for); new §9.1
  "Common pitfalls" lists the silent-failure modes a plugin
  author actually hits: unsigned placeholders, single-segment
  wildcard surprises, `card_key` ↔ `card_key_path` mismatch,
  template/script field mismatches, missing `registerPlugin()`,
  hostPreview fallbacks, action-POST body shape surprises.

+- `platform.network.fetch(url, init)` — works, gated by `declaredEndpoints` glob match. Contract documented in §3.1 below.
 - `platform.showNotification`, `platform.storage`, `platform.camera`, `platform.gallery`, `platform.file`, `platform.location`, `platform.message.respond` — *reject* with a clear error in V1 inbox mode. For V1 dogfood, stick to `network.fetch`.
 
+### 3.1 `declaredEndpoints` glob syntax
+
+`declaredEndpoints` controls which URLs your plugin may pass to `platform.network.fetch`. The host (both Android `EndpointMatcher.kt` and the TS SDK's `network.ts`) implements the same glob grammar:
+
+- A literal `*` matches **exactly one segment**, never multiple. The boundary changes by position:
+  - In the host portion of the URL (before the first `/` after the scheme), `*` matches `[^./]*` — a single host label. `https://*.example.com/feed` matches `https://api.example.com/feed`, but **not** `https://a.b.example.com/feed`.
+  - In the path portion, `*` matches `[^/]*` — a single path segment. `https://example.com/api/*` matches `https://example.com/api/v1`, but **not** `https://example.com/api/v1/users`.
+- There is no `**` for "any number of segments." You need one entry per depth, or you need to make the path component a single segment (e.g. encode trailing path in a query string).
+- Match is anchored: the full URL must match, including query string. To allow a query, include `*` in the path or query position.
+
+Example: to allow both `/api/v1/ack` and `/api/v2/ack`, declare both: `["https://example.com/api/v1/*", "https://example.com/api/v2/*"]`. Or, if you don't care about path depth, declare `["https://example.com/api/*", "https://example.com/api/*/*"]` and so on.
+
+This is the single most common manifest mistake — a plugin author declares `https://example.com/api/*` and then `fetch`-es `https://example.com/api/v1/users`, which gets rejected with `endpoint_not_declared`. The same pattern controls **template action endpoints** (the publish-time validator uses the same matcher to verify `action.endpoint` is in `endpoints`).
+
+### 3.2 `platform.network.fetch` contract
+
+The host bridge wraps a stock OkHttp client. Behavior:
+
+- **Returns a `Response`** for any HTTP response (2xx, 4xx, 5xx all resolve). The status is on `response.status`. You're responsible for checking it.
+- **Throws** on:
+  - `endpoint_not_declared` — URL doesn't match any `declaredEndpoints` glob (see §3.1).
+  - `cleartext_in_release` — `http://` URL in a release build. Debug builds allow cleartext for LAN dev.
+  - Network failures (DNS, connection refused, timeout) propagate as an `Error` whose message includes the underlying cause; treat them like a generic offline state.
+- **Timeouts**: OkHttp library defaults (no explicit override). That's ~10s connect / 10s read each. If your endpoint can be slow, factor that into your UX (the user is staring at the card).
+- **Request shape**: standard `RequestInit` subset. `method`, `headers`, `body` (string), `contentType` are forwarded. No streaming bodies, no `AbortController` in V1.
+- **Cookies are disabled** at the bridge (`CookieJar.NO_COOKIES`). Authenticate via headers or signed bodies.
+
+```ts
+try {
+  const response = await platform.network.fetch('https://example.com/api/ack', {
+    method: 'POST',
+    headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },
+    body: JSON.stringify({ item_id: itemId }),
+  });
+  if (!response.ok) {
+    // 4xx/5xx — your backend rejected the action. Show an error in the card.
+    return;
+  }
+  // 2xx — success.
+} catch (err) {
+  // endpoint not declared, cleartext in release, offline, timeout, etc.
+  // The exception message is human-readable; surface it or fall back to a
+  // generic "couldn't reach server" state.
+}
+```
+

+## 9. Common server errors
+
+The server returned a 4xx or 5xx; here's what to change.
 
 - **`401 invalid envelope signature`** — your sender's Ed25519 key doesn't match the one registered. Re-check `private_key_path`.
 - **`410 plugin missing, revoked, or not owned by sender`** — `plugin_id` (the row UUID) is wrong, or you accidentally used `plugin_identifier`. The two are distinct (see §5 vs §6).
@@ -505,13 +553,23 @@ def action():
 - **`400 expires_at exceeds the 48h live-card cap`** (cards upsert) — your supplied `expires_at` is more than 48 hours from now. Live cards are capped server-side to prevent slot squatting. Send shorter and re-upsert to extend.
 - **`400 expires_at is not in the future`** (cards upsert) — you sent an already-expired `expires_at`. Use a future timestamp.
 - **`409 sequence_number not greater than existing`** (cards upsert) — the existing card has a `sequence_number` ≥ what you sent. Sequence must be strictly increasing per `card_key`.
-- **Card shows "render failed: plugin did not install __syncler_internal_dispatch — missing registerPlugin() call?"** — your bundle defined the plugin class but didn't call `registerPlugin(new YourPlugin())` at module scope. See §3.
-- **Card shows "endpoint not declared"** — your `onclick` handler is calling a URL that doesn't match any pattern in your manifest's `declaredEndpoints`. Add the URL pattern (globs allowed: `https://example.com/api/*`) and re-publish.
 - **`HostPreviewValidationError: hostPreview.X is N UTF-8 bytes; max is M`** — caught at `client.send_to` time. Trim the offending field; see §2 for the caps. UTF-8 byte counts, not characters — emoji and accented characters cost more than one byte.
-- **Row shows "New message from {sender}" with fallback text only** — your message was sent without a `hostPreview` block, or the block was malformed (logged + ignored on the device). The detail view still loads the plugin and renders normally; only the row is generic. Add a valid `hostPreview` and re-send.
+- **`422 manifest validation failed`** (cards/plugins publish) — Pydantic rejected the manifest body. The detail field tells you which check failed. Most common: `template required when renderer == 'template'`, `card_key_path required when card_type == 'live'`, `action endpoint not allowed by declared endpoints`. Mirror this validation client-side via `validatePluginManifest` (TS SDK) to catch before the round-trip.
 
 Cross-reference `docs/crypto-spec.md` for the AAD + envelope canonical byte shapes if signatures disagree.
 
+## 9.1 Common pitfalls
+
+These pass server-side validation but bite you at runtime. The SDK validator catches most of them now; check here first when something compiles and publishes but doesn't behave.
+
+- **`UNSIGNED-PLACEHOLDER-REPLACE-WITH-SIGN-BUNDLE` in `bundleHash` / `signature`.** You forgot to run `sign-bundle.ts` on the built bundle. The SDK validator rejects this (post Phase 4.1) — `bundleHash` must be exactly 64 lowercase hex chars (SHA-256), `signature` must be exactly 128 hex chars (Ed25519). If the SDK lets it through, the server rejects at publish with 422; if both let it through, the device fails the manifest-hash check and shows "Plugin not loaded."
+- **`registerPlugin()` not called.** Card shows *"render failed: plugin did not install __syncler_internal_dispatch — missing registerPlugin() call?"*. Your bundle defined the plugin class but never called `registerPlugin(new YourPlugin())` at module scope. The host's bundle loader looks for the dispatcher hook the SDK installs from `registerPlugin`; without it, there's nothing to dispatch into.
+- **Single-segment wildcard surprise in `declaredEndpoints`.** `https://example.com/api/*` matches `https://example.com/api/v1` but NOT `https://example.com/api/v1/users`. `*` is one segment, never multiple. Card shows *"endpoint not declared"*. See §3.1 for the full glob grammar.
+- **`card_key` doesn't match `card_key_path` resolved on the plaintext.** The manifest declares `card_key_path: "$.order_id"`; the device extracts that on decrypt and uses it as the merge key. You pass `card_key="order-456"` to `upsert_card`. If the plaintext's `$.order_id` doesn't equal `"order-456"`, the device treats each upsert as a separate row — your "live" card behaves like an event card. The server doesn't cross-check; it's your responsibility.
+- **Template/script field mismatches.** Setting `template: {...}` on a `renderer: "script"` manifest, or omitting `template` on `renderer: "template"`. SDK validator catches both. Same with `cardType: "live"` requiring `cardKeyPath` and `cardType: "event"` rejecting it. If the SDK validator misses a case you hit, file a Phase 4.5 doc-bug.
+- **Row shows "New message from {sender}" with fallback text only.** Your message was sent without a `hostPreview` block, or the block was malformed (logged + ignored on the device). The detail view still loads the plugin and renders normally; only the row is generic. Add a valid `hostPreview` and re-send.
+- **Action POST body shape surprise.** Script renderer: your `onclick` builds whatever body you want. Template renderer: the host POSTs the **entire decrypted payload** verbatim, with no Authorization header. If your endpoint expects `{item_id, acted_at}` and you swapped to template renderer, the endpoint now sees the full payload — adjust the receiver, don't fight the host.
+
 ## 10. Versioning + history
 
 Publish every plugin release as a new row under the same `plugin_identifier`. `plugin_identifier` is the stable name, while `plugin_row_id` is the exact version row returned by `client.publish_plugin(...)`.

-Build the example bundle:
+Build the example bundle, then sign it, then validate:
 
 ```sh
-npm run build:example
+npm run build:example                                             # writes examples/minimal/dist/plugin.bundle.js
+npx tsx tools/sign-bundle.ts \
+  examples/minimal/dist/plugin.bundle.js \
+  ~/.syncler/keys/sender.pem \
+  examples/minimal/manifest.json \
+  examples/minimal/manifest.signed.json
 ```
 
+The signer reads the unsigned `manifest.json`, computes SHA-256 over the bundle, signs `(canonical manifest || bundleHash)` with Ed25519, and writes `manifest.signed.json` with `bundleHash` + `signature` populated. That signed manifest is what passes `validatePluginManifest` and what your backend ships to `client.publish_plugin(...)`.
+
 The native host calls `__syncler_internal_dispatch(hook, args)` after loading the plugin bundle. Plugin bundles should register exactly one plugin instance with `registerPlugin`.

.\sdk-plugin\examples\minimal\README.md:38:`bundleHash: 'UNSIGNED-PLACEHOLDER-REPLACE-WITH-SIGN-BUNDLE'` (and the same for `signature`) is deliberate: the SDK's `validatePluginManifest` rejects this as-written (requires 64-hex `bundleHash` + 128-hex `signature`). That's by design — an unsigned manifest can't be published. The placeholder is loud rather than `'00'` so the failure mode is obvious if you forget step 2.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:36:- **Per-device dismiss (server-side filter).** When the user dismisses a message on device A, `/v1/messages/{id}/dismiss` writes a `DeliveryStatus` row keyed on `(message_id, device_id=A)`. Subsequent calls to `/v1/messages/inbox` from device A LEFT JOIN `DeliveryStatus` for `device_id=A` and filter rows where `dismissed_at IS NOT NULL` out of A's feed. The dismiss SSE event still fans out to *all* of the user's devices, but the server-side filter is per-device — devices B, C, etc. receive the hint and refresh, but their own feeds keep the row until they dismiss it themselves. V1 design: dismiss is a per-device gesture (some users want a card visible elsewhere); cross-device "dismiss everywhere" is a V1.5 add.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:74:`searchText` is folded into the host's inbox search alongside title, subtitle, summary, and sender name. The host does a case-insensitive substring match — populate this with the terms a user would type into the search box but that aren't part of the visible row (ticker symbols, ticket numbers, account references). Plugin-scoped *content* search (a search bar that runs against your backend) is V1.5.

.\docs\integration-guide.md:196:The host bridge wraps a stock OkHttp client. Behavior:
.\docs\integration-guide.md:202:  - Network failures (DNS, connection refused, timeout) propagate as an `Error` whose message includes the underlying cause; treat them like a generic offline state.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:203:- **Timeouts**: OkHttp library defaults (no explicit override). That's ~10s connect / 10s read each. If your endpoint can be slow, factor that into your UX (the user is staring at the card).
.\docs\integration-guide.md:204:- **Request shape**: standard `RequestInit` subset. `method`, `headers`, `body` (string), `contentType` are forwarded. No streaming bodies, no `AbortController` in V1.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:205:- **Cookies are disabled** at the bridge (`CookieJar.NO_COOKIES`). Authenticate via headers or signed bodies.

.\docs\integration-guide.md:444:`user_id` is **required**. The canonical signed envelope binds `(sender_id, user_id, card_key)` — without `user_id` in the signature, an attacker (or a coincidence: two users with the same `card_key` under the same sender) could be deleted by mistake. The delete endpoint matches exactly that triple in the row lookup.

.\docs\integration-guide.md:565:- **`UNSIGNED-PLACEHOLDER-REPLACE-WITH-SIGN-BUNDLE` in `bundleHash` / `signature`.** You forgot to run `sign-bundle.ts` on the built bundle. The SDK validator rejects this (post Phase 4.1) — `bundleHash` must be exactly 64 lowercase hex chars (SHA-256), `signature` must be exactly 128 hex chars (Ed25519). If the SDK lets it through, the server rejects at publish with 422; if both let it through, the device fails the manifest-hash check and shows "Plugin not loaded."

.\docs\crypto-spec.md:150:### Message Envelope (Ed25519 sender signature input)
.\docs\crypto-spec.md:156:The sender signs the canonical envelope JSON with Ed25519. The server reconstructs the envelope from the request fields and verifies against the registered sender's public key. Envelope is also what the recipient device uses to verify the signature on inbox fetch — therefore inbox/detail responses include `expires_at` (in addition to the body, nonce, signature).

.\docs\crypto-spec.md:218:The V1 server performs a per-sender in-memory LRU replay check for the last 100,000 nonces. This protects the current server process only. A Redis or database-backed replay check is planned for V1.5.
.\docs\crypto-spec.md:246:Canonical JSON for the sender's `envelope_signature` on `POST /v1/cards/upsert`:
.\docs\crypto-spec.md:276:**`user_id` is REQUIRED in the envelope.** Without it, a delete signature valid for one user's card could be replayed against another user's card with a coincidentally matching `(sender_id, card_key)` — the table is uniquely keyed on `(sender_id, user_id, card_key)`, so the lookup would otherwise be ambiguous. (Codex consultation 62 security finding.) The server matches the exact triple before deleting; mismatched triples no-op silently and still publish a `card.delete` SSE event so all of the user's devices clear any stale local copy.

.\docs\ROADMAP.md:30:6. **Automated pairing handshake.** Today the user reads `user_id` + `pairing_key_hex` off the device confirmation screen and types them into the sender's backend. V1.5 wires the bootstrap exchange end-to-end: the device POSTs the `(user_id, pairing_key)` tuple to a sender-supplied broker URL embedded in the QR; the sender's backend polls a `did the user complete this token?` endpoint and unlocks `set_pairing` automatically. Removes the largest first-impressions papercut. See `sdk-python/README.md` Quickstart for the V1 dogfood flow this replaces.

.\sdk-plugin\examples\minimal\README.md:38:`bundleHash: 'UNSIGNED-PLACEHOLDER-REPLACE-WITH-SIGN-BUNDLE'` (and the same for `signature`) is deliberate: the SDK's `validatePluginManifest` rejects this as-written (requires 64-hex `bundleHash` + 128-hex `signature`). That's by design — an unsigned manifest can't be published. The placeholder is loud rather than `'00'` so the failure mode is obvious if you forget step 2.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:36:- **Per-device dismiss (server-side filter).** When the user dismisses a message on device A, `/v1/messages/{id}/dismiss` writes a `DeliveryStatus` row keyed on `(message_id, device_id=A)`. Subsequent calls to `/v1/messages/inbox` from device A LEFT JOIN `DeliveryStatus` for `device_id=A` and filter rows where `dismissed_at IS NOT NULL` out of A's feed. The dismiss SSE event still fans out to *all* of the user's devices, but the server-side filter is per-device — devices B, C, etc. receive the hint and refresh, but their own feeds keep the row until they dismiss it themselves. V1 design: dismiss is a per-device gesture (some users want a card visible elsewhere); cross-device "dismiss everywhere" is a V1.5 add.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:74:`searchText` is folded into the host's inbox search alongside title, subtitle, summary, and sender name. The host does a case-insensitive substring match — populate this with the terms a user would type into the search box but that aren't part of the visible row (ticker symbols, ticket numbers, account references). Plugin-scoped *content* search (a search bar that runs against your backend) is V1.5.

.\docs\integration-guide.md:444:`user_id` is **required**. .\docs\crypto-spec.md:156:The sender signs the canonical envelope JSON with Ed25519. .\docs\crypto-spec.md:276:**`user_id` is REQUIRED in the envelope.** Without it, a delete signature valid for one user's card could be replayed against another user's card with a coincidentally matching `(sender_id, card_key)` — the table is uniquely keyed on `(sender_id, user_id, card_key)`, so the lookup would otherwise be ambiguous. (Codex consultation 62 security finding.) The server matches the exact triple before deleting; mismatched triples no-op silently and still publish a `card.delete` SSE event so all of the user's devices clear any stale local copy.

   1: package app.syncler.android.pluginhost
   2: 
   3: object EndpointMatcher {
   4:     fun matches(url: String, patterns: List<String>): Boolean =
   5:         patterns.any { pattern -> endpointPatternToRegex(pattern).matches(url) }
   6: 
   7:     private fun endpointPatternToRegex(pattern: String): Regex {
   8:         val pathStart = findPathStart(pattern)
   9:         val source = buildString {
  10:             pattern.forEachIndexed { index, character ->
  11:                 if (character == '*') {
  12:                     append(if (index < pathStart) "[^./]*" else "[^/]*")
  13:                 } else {
  14:                     append(Regex.escape(character.toString()))
  15:                 }
  16:             }
  17:         }
  18:         return Regex("^$source$")
  19:     }
  20: 
  21:     private fun findPathStart(pattern: String): Int {
  22:         val schemeEnd = pattern.indexOf("://")
  23:         val searchFrom = if (schemeEnd == -1) 0 else schemeEnd + 3
  24:         val slash = pattern.indexOf('/', searchFrom)
  25:         return if (slash == -1) pattern.length else slash
  26:     }
  27: }

   1: import { getRegisteredManifest } from './manifest';
   2: import { callPlatform } from './platform';
   3: 
   4: /**
   5:  * Error raised when a URL does not match the plugin manifest endpoint allowlist.
   6:  */
   7: export class EndpointNotDeclaredError extends Error {
   8:   /** URL rejected before reaching the native bridge. */
   9:   readonly url: string;
  10: 
  11:   constructor(url: string) {
  12:     super(`Endpoint is not declared by plugin manifest: ${url}`);
  13:     this.name = 'EndpointNotDeclaredError';
  14:     this.url = url;
  15:   }
  16: }
  17: 
  18: /**
  19:  * Typed wrapper for `platform.network`.
  20:  */
  21: export const network = {
  22:   /**
  23:    * Fetches a URL through the host bridge after checking the manifest endpoint allowlist.
  24:    */
  25:   async fetch(url: string, init?: RequestInit): Promise<Response> {
  26:     assertEndpointDeclared(url);
  27:     return await callPlatform('network.fetch', (bridge) => bridge.network.fetch(url, init));
  28:   },
  29: };
  30: 
  31: /**
  32:  * Returns true when a URL matches at least one declared endpoint pattern.
  33:  */
  34: export function isEndpointDeclared(url: string, patterns: readonly string[]): boolean {
  35:   return patterns.some((pattern) => endpointPatternToRegExp(pattern).test(url));
  36: }
  37: 
  38: /**
  39:  * Throws `EndpointNotDeclaredError` when the active plugin manifest does not declare a URL.
  40:  */
  41: export function assertEndpointDeclared(url: string): void {
  42:   const manifest = getRegisteredManifest();
  43:   if (!manifest || !isEndpointDeclared(url, manifest.declaredEndpoints)) {
  44:     throw new EndpointNotDeclaredError(url);
  45:   }
  46: }
  47: 
  48: function endpointPatternToRegExp(pattern: string): RegExp {
  49:   const pathStart = findPathStart(pattern);
  50:   let source = '';
  51: 
  52:   for (let index = 0; index < pattern.length; index += 1) {
  53:     const character = pattern[index];
  54:     if (character === '*') {
  55:       source += index < pathStart ? '[^./]*' : '[^/]*';
  56:     } else {
  57:       source += escapeRegExp(character);
  58:     }
  59:   }
  60: 
  61:   return new RegExp(`^${source}$`);
  62: }
  63: 
  64: function findPathStart(pattern: string): number {
  65:   const schemeEnd = pattern.indexOf('://');
  66:   const searchFrom = schemeEnd === -1 ? 0 : schemeEnd + 3;
  67:   const slash = pattern.indexOf('/', searchFrom);
  68:   return slash === -1 ? pattern.length : slash;
  69: }
  70: 
  71: function escapeRegExp(character: string | undefined): string {
  72:   if (!character) return '';
  73:   return /[.+?^${}()|[\]\\]/.test(character) ? `\\${character}` : character;
  74: }

   9: import kotlinx.coroutines.withContext

  17: class NetworkBridge(
  18:     httpClient: OkHttpClient? = null,
  19:     private val auditLogger: AuditLogger,
  20: ) {
  21:     private val client = httpClient ?: OkHttpClient.Builder()
  22:         .cookieJar(CookieJar.NO_COOKIES)
  23:         .connectionSpecs(
  24:             if (BuildConfig.DEBUG) {
  25:                 listOf(ConnectionSpec.MODERN_TLS, ConnectionSpec.CLEARTEXT)
  26:             } else {
  27:                 listOf(ConnectionSpec.MODERN_TLS)
  28:             },
  29:         )
  30:         .build()
  31: 
  32:     suspend fun fetch(plugin: PluginInstance, argsJson: String): String = withContext(Dispatchers.IO) {
  33:         val args = JsonBridgeCodec.objectFrom(argsJson)
  34:         val url = args["url"] as? String ?: return@withContext JsonBridgeCodec.error("invalid_args")
  35:         // Bridge-level scheme check: defense in depth against an injected
  36:         // OkHttpClient whose connectionSpecs might not align with this
  37:         // bridge's release-HTTPS policy. Enforcing scheme here means we
  38:         // fail closed regardless of how `client` was built.
  39:         val schemeOk = url.startsWith("https://") || (BuildConfig.DEBUG && url.startsWith("http://"))
  40:         if (!schemeOk) {
  41:             auditLogger.denied(plugin.manifest.id, "cleartext_in_release", url)
  42:             throw PluginBridgeException("cleartext_in_release", "fetch URL must be HTTPS")
  43:         }
  44:         if (!EndpointMatcher.matches(url, plugin.manifest.declaredEndpoints)) {
  45:             auditLogger.denied(plugin.manifest.id, "endpoint_not_declared", url)
  46:             throw PluginBridgeException("endpoint_not_declared", "Endpoint not declared: $url")
  47:         }
  48: 
  49:         val init = args["init"] as? Map<*, *>
  50:         val method = (init?.get("method") as? String)?.uppercase() ?: "GET"
  51:         val body = init?.get("body") as? String
  52:         val mediaType = (init?.get("contentType") as? String)?.toMediaTypeOrNull()
  53:         val requestBody = if (body != null && method !in setOf("GET", "HEAD")) body.toRequestBody(mediaType) else null
  54:         val builder = Request.Builder().url(url).method(method, requestBody)
  55:         (init?.get("headers") as? Map<*, *>)?.forEach { (name, value) ->
  56:             if (name is String && value is String) builder.header(name, value)
  57:         }
  58: 
  59:         client.newCall(builder.build()).execute().use { response ->
  60:             JsonBridgeCodec.toJson(
  61:                 mapOf(
  62:                     "status" to response.code,
  63:                     "headers" to response.headers.toMultimap().mapValues { it.value.joinToString(",") },
  64:                     "body" to (response.body?.string() ?: ""),
  65:                 ),
  66:             )
  67:         }
  68:     }
  69: }

  13: import app.syncler.android.pluginhost.capabilities.NotificationBridge
  14: import app.syncler.android.pluginhost.capabilities.StorageBridge
  15: import kotlinx.coroutines.CoroutineScope
  16: import kotlinx.coroutines.launch
  17: import kotlinx.coroutines.withTimeout
  18: 
  19: class PluginBridge(
  20:     private val plugin: PluginInstance,
  21:     private val webViewProvider: () -> WebView?,
  22:     private val scope: CoroutineScope,
  23:     private val networkBridge: NetworkBridge,
  24:     private val storageBridge: StorageBridge,
  25:     private val notificationBridge: NotificationBridge,
  26:     private val cameraBridge: CameraBridge,
  27:     private val galleryBridge: GalleryBridge,
  28:     private val fileBridge: FileBridge,
  29:     private val locationBridge: LocationBridge,
  30:     private val messageBridge: MessageBridge,
  31:     private val auditLogger: AuditLogger,
  32: ) {
  33:     private val mainHandler = Handler(Looper.getMainLooper())
  34: 
  35:     @JavascriptInterface
  36:     fun call(method: String, argsJson: String, callbackId: String) {
  37:         scope.launch {
  38:             val resultJson = runCatching {
  39:                 withTimeout(CALL_TIMEOUT_MS) {
  40:                     bridgeSuccessJson(dispatch(method, argsJson))
  41:                 }
  42:             }.getOrElse { error ->
  43:                 val reason = when (error) {
  44:                     is kotlinx.coroutines.TimeoutCancellationException -> "timeout"
  45:                     is PluginBridgeException -> error.code
  46:                     else -> "bridge_error"
  47:                 }
  48:                 auditLogger.denied(plugin.manifest.id, reason, method)
  49:                 bridgeErrorJson(reason, error.message ?: reason)
  50:             }
  51:             deliver(callbackId, resultJson)
  52:         }
  53:     }
  54: 
  55:     private suspend fun dispatch(method: String, argsJson: String): String {
  56:         val capability = requiredCapability(method)
  57:         if (capability != null && capability !in plugin.grantedCapabilities) {
  58:             auditLogger.denied(plugin.manifest.id, "capability_not_granted", capability)
  59:             throw PluginBridgeException("capability_not_granted", "Capability not granted: $capability")
  60:         }
  61: 
  62:         return when (method) {
  63:             "platform.network.fetch" -> networkBridge.fetch(plugin, argsJson)
  64:             "platform.storage.get" -> storageBridge.get(plugin, argsJson)
  65:             "platform.storage.set" -> storageBridge.set(plugin, argsJson)
  66:             "platform.storage.delete" -> storageBridge.delete(plugin, argsJson)
  67:             "platform.showNotification" -> notificationBridge.show(plugin, argsJson)
  68:             "platform.camera.capture" -> cameraBridge.capture(plugin, argsJson)
  69:             "platform.gallery.pick" -> galleryBridge.pick(plugin, argsJson)
  70:             "platform.file.pick" -> fileBridge.pick(plugin, argsJson)
  71:             "platform.location.current" -> locationBridge.current(plugin, argsJson)
  72:             "platform.message.respond" -> messageBridge.respond(plugin, argsJson)
  73:             "platform.message.dismissBehavior" -> messageBridge.dismissBehavior(plugin, argsJson)
  74:             else -> {
  75:                 auditLogger.denied(plugin.manifest.id, "unknown_method", method)
  76:                 throw PluginBridgeException("unknown_method", "Unknown bridge method: $method")
  77:             }
  78:         }
  79:     }
  80: 
  81:     private fun deliver(callbackId: String, resultJson: String) {
  82:         val script = "window.__syncler_internal_callback(${JsonEscaping.quote(callbackId)}, $resultJson)"
  83:         mainHandler.post {
  84:             runCatching { webViewProvider()?.evaluateJavascript(script, null) }
  85:                 .onFailure { auditLogger.denied(plugin.manifest.id, "callback_delivery_failed", it.message) }
  86:         }
  87:     }
  88: 
  89:     companion object {
  90:         const val NATIVE_BRIDGE_NAME = "__syncler_native__"
  91:         const val CALL_TIMEOUT_MS = 30_000L
  92:     }
  93: }
  94: 
  95: internal fun requiredCapability(method: String): String? = when {
  96:     method.startsWith("platform.network.") -> "network"
  97:     method.startsWith("platform.storage.") -> "storage"
  98:     method.startsWith("platform.camera.") -> "camera"
  99:     method.startsWith("platform.gallery.") -> "gallery"
 100:     method.startsWith("platform.file.") -> "file"
 101:     method.startsWith("platform.location.") -> "location"
 102:     method == "platform.showNotification" -> null
 103:     method.startsWith("platform.message.") -> null
 104:     else -> null
 105: }
 106: 
 107: internal fun bridgeSuccessJson(valueJson: String): String =
 108:     """{"success":true,"value":$valueJson}"""
 109: 
 110: internal fun bridgeErrorJson(error: String, message: String): String =
 111:     """{"success":false,"error":${JsonEscaping.quote(error)},"message":${JsonEscaping.quote(message)}}"""

 185:  * specific JWT, ג€¦); the host just attests to the user's tap.
 186:  *
 187:  * SECURITY: this builds its OWN [OkHttpClient] rather than injecting the
 188:  * `:core:network` singleton. That singleton has an `AuthTokenProvider`-backed

 191:  * would auto-attach the user's Syncler bearer JWT to every request. Template

 193:  * globs) and must never see the user's host-auth token ג€” otherwise a
 194:  * compromised or hostile sender could exfiltrate it from a single tap.
 195:  * Closes Codex consultation 62 RED #1.
 196:  *
 197:  * Pattern mirrors [app.syncler.android.pluginhost.capabilities.NetworkBridge],
 198:  * which also builds its own unauthenticated client for the same reason on
 199:  * the WebView-based renderer path.
 200:  */
 201: @Singleton
 202: class TemplateActionRunner @Inject constructor() {
 203:     private val httpClient: OkHttpClient by lazy {
 204:         OkHttpClient.Builder()
 205:             .connectionSpecs(
 206:                 if (BuildConfig.DEBUG) {
 207:                     listOf(ConnectionSpec.MODERN_TLS, ConnectionSpec.CLEARTEXT)
 208:                 } else {
 209:                     listOf(ConnectionSpec.MODERN_TLS)
 210:                 },
 211:             )
 212:             .build()
 213:     }
 214: 
 215:     suspend fun post(endpoint: String, payloadJson: String) {
 216:         withContext(Dispatchers.IO) {
 217:             // Release builds reject cleartext outright. NetworkBridge does
 218:             // the same check; we mirror it here so a leaked-template
 219:             // manifest with an http:// endpoint can't fall through to a
 220:             // cleartext POST on production.
 221:             val schemeOk = endpoint.startsWith("https://") ||
 222:                 (BuildConfig.DEBUG && endpoint.startsWith("http://"))
 223:             if (!schemeOk) {
 224:                 Timber.tag(TAG).w("template action POST %s blocked: non-HTTPS", endpoint)
 225:                 return@withContext
 226:             }
 227:             runCatching {
 228:                 val request = Request.Builder()
 229:                     .url(endpoint)
 230:                     .post(payloadJson.toRequestBody(JSON_MEDIA))
 231:                     .build()
 232:                 httpClient.newCall(request).execute().use { response ->
 233:                     if (!response.isSuccessful) {
 234:                         Timber.tag(TAG).w(
 235:                             "template action POST %s failed: HTTP %d",
 236:                             endpoint,
 237:                             response.code,
 238:                         )
 239:                     } else {
 240:                         Timber.tag(TAG).i("template action POST %s ok", endpoint)
 241:                     }
 242:                 }
 243:             }.onFailure {
 244:                 Timber.tag(TAG).w(it, "template action POST %s threw", endpoint)
 245:             }
 246:         }
 247:     }
 248: 
 249:     private companion object {
 250:         val JSON_MEDIA = "application/json".toMediaType()
 251:     }
 252: }
 253:

 119: /**
 120:  * Error raised when the native bridge is unavailable or rejects a call.
 121:  */
 122: export class PlatformError extends Error {
 123:   /** Original rejection reason, when present. */
 124:   readonly cause: unknown;
 125: 
 126:   constructor(message: string, cause?: unknown) {
 127:     super(message);
 128:     this.name = 'PlatformError';
 129:     this.cause = cause;
 130:   }
 131: }
 132: 
 133: /**
 134:  * Returns the host-injected bridge or throws a typed error when unavailable.
 135:  */
 136: export function getPlatformBridge(): PlatformBridge {
 137:   const injected = globalThis.platform ?? globalThis.window?.platform;
 138:   if (!injected) {
 139:     throw new PlatformError('Syncler platform bridge is not available');
 140:   }
 141:   return injected;
 142: }
 143: 
 144: /**
 145:  * Wraps an async platform call and normalizes bridge rejections.
 146:  */
 147: export async function callPlatform<T>(operation: string, callback: (bridge: PlatformBridge) => Promise<T>): Promise<T> {
 148:   try {
 149:     return await callback(getPlatformBridge());
 150:   } catch (error) {
 151:     if (error instanceof PlatformError) {
 152:       throw error;
 153:     }
 154:     throw new PlatformError(`Syncler platform operation failed: ${operation}`, error);
 155:   }
 156: }
 157: 
 158: /**
 159:  * Wraps a sync platform call and normalizes bridge failures.
 160:  */
 161: export function callPlatformSync<T>(operation: string, callback: (bridge: PlatformBridge) => T): T {
 162:   try {
 163:     return callback(getPlatformBridge());
 164:   } catch (error) {
 165:     if (error instanceof PlatformError) {
 166:       throw error;
 167:     }
 168:     throw new PlatformError(`Syncler platform operation failed: ${operation}`, error);
 169:   }
 170: }

  79: /**
  80:  * Error raised when plugin manifest validation fails.
  81:  */
  82: export class ManifestValidationError extends Error {
  83:   /** Individual validation failures. */
  84:   readonly issues: string[];
  85: 
  86:   constructor(issues: string[]) {
  87:     super(`Invalid plugin manifest: ${issues.join('; ')}`);
  88:     this.name = 'ManifestValidationError';
  89:     this.issues = issues;
  90:   }
  91: }
  92: 
  93: const idPattern = /^[a-zA-Z][a-zA-Z0-9-]*(\.[a-zA-Z][a-zA-Z0-9-]*)+$/;
  94: const semverPattern = /^(0|[1-9]\d*)\.(0|[1-9]\d*)\.(0|[1-9]\d*)(?:-[0-9A-Za-z.-]+)?(?:\+[0-9A-Za-z.-]+)?$/;
  95: const hexPattern = /^[0-9a-fA-F]+$/;
  96: const allCapabilities = new Set<string>(Object.values(Capability));
  97: const allDismissBehaviors = new Set<string>(Object.values(DismissBehavior));
  98:

 100: 
 101: /**
 102:  * Returns true when `value` is a valid plugin manifest.
 103:  */
 104: export function isPluginManifest(value: unknown): value is PluginManifest {
 105:   return validatePluginManifest(value).valid;
 106: }
 107: 
 108: /**
 109:  * Validates unknown JSON-like data as a `PluginManifest`.
 110:  */
 111: export function validatePluginManifest(value: unknown): { valid: true; manifest: PluginManifest } | { valid: false; issues: string[] } {
 112:   const issues: string[] = [];
 113: 
 114:   if (!isRecord(value)) {
 115:     return { valid: false, issues: ['manifest must be an object'] };
 116:   }
 117: 
 118:   requireString(value, 'id', issues, (id) => {
 119:     if (!idPattern.test(id)) issues.push('id must be reverse-DNS format');
 120:   });
 121:   requireString(value, 'name', issues);
 122:   requireString(value, 'version', issues, (version) => {
 123:     if (!semverPattern.test(version)) issues.push('version must be semver');
 124:   });
 125:   requireString(value, 'senderId', issues);
 126:   // bundleHash is SHA-256 of the bundle bytes ג†’ 32 bytes ג†’ 64 hex chars.
 127:   // signature is Ed25519 over (canonical manifest || bundleHash) ג†’ 64 bytes
 128:   // ג†’ 128 hex chars. The previous "any hex" check let "00" or any other
 129:   // placeholder through validation, which authors hit constantly: the
 130:   // server rejects at publish time with a 422, but the SDK should have
 131:   // caught it locally. (External DX review, lottery-claude, Phase 4.1 #1.)
 132:   requireString(value, 'bundleHash', issues, (hash) => {
 133:     if (!hexPattern.test(hash)) {
 134:       issues.push('bundleHash must be hex');
 135:     } else if (hash.length !== 64) {
 136:       issues.push(
 137:         'bundleHash must be 64 lowercase hex chars (SHA-256). ' +
 138:           'Run sign-bundle.ts on your built bundle to populate this field.',
 139:       );
 140:     }
 141:   });
 142:   requireString(value, 'signature', issues, (signature) => {
 143:     if (!hexPattern.test(signature)) {
 144:       issues.push('signature must be hex');
 145:     } else if (signature.length !== 128) {
 146:       issues.push(
 147:         'signature must be 128 hex chars (Ed25519, 64 bytes). ' +
 148:           'Run sign-bundle.ts on your built bundle to populate this field.',
 149:       );
 150:     }
 151:   });
 152:   requireString(value, 'minPlatformVersion', issues, (version) => {
 153:     if (!semverPattern.test(version)) issues.push('minPlatformVersion must be semver');
 154:   });
 155: 
 156:   // renderer + template pairing. Both are optional; server defaults
 157:   // renderer to 'script'. When present, renderer must be one of the
 158:   // two enum values, and template/script ג†” template-present pairing
 159:   // is enforced strictly (matches server's

   1: /**
   2:  * Sign a plugin bundle for Syncler.
   3:  *
   4:  * The Android host verifies the signature over
   5:  *   canonical_manifest_without_signature  ||  bundleHash_raw_bytes
   6:  * per ``docs/crypto-spec.md`` ֲ§5. This tool computes the bundle hash,
   7:  * inserts it into the manifest, computes the canonical bytes the same
   8:  * way Android does, signs those, and writes the signature back into
   9:  * the manifest.
  10:  *
  11:  * Usage: tsx tools/sign-bundle.ts <bundle.js> <ed25519_private_key.pem> <manifest.json> [output.signed.json]
  12:  */

  63:  * Canonical JSON with sorted keys, no whitespace, ASCII-escape non-ASCII.
  64:  * Matches ``server/app/crypto/signatures.py:canonical_manifest_for_signing``
  65:  * and ``android/.../PluginSignatureVerifier.kt:canonicalJson`` byte-for-byte
  66:  * given equivalent inputs.
  67:  */
  68: function canonicalJson(value: unknown): string {
  69:   if (value === null) return 'null';
  70:   if (typeof value === 'boolean') return value ? 'true' : 'false';
  71:   if (typeof value === 'number') {
  72:     if (!Number.isFinite(value)) throw new Error('JSON numbers must be finite');
  73:     return Number.isInteger(value) ? String(value) : String(value);
  74:   }
  75:   if (typeof value === 'string') return quote(value);
  76:   if (Array.isArray(value)) {
  77:     return '[' + value.map(canonicalJson).join(',') + ']';
  78:   }
  79:   if (typeof value === 'object') {
  80:     const keys = Object.keys(value as object).sort();
  81:     return (
  82:       '{' +
  83:       keys
  84:         .map((k) => quote(k) + ':' + canonicalJson((value as Record<string, unknown>)[k]))
  85:         .join(',') +
  86:       '}'
  87:     );
  88:   }
  89:   throw new Error(`Unsupported value type: ${typeof value}`);
  90: }

   1: package app.syncler.feature.inbox
   2: 
   3: import android.webkit.JavascriptInterface
   4: import android.webkit.WebView
   5: import app.syncler.feature.inbox.BuildConfig
   6: import kotlinx.coroutines.CoroutineScope

   8: import kotlinx.coroutines.SupervisorJob
   9: import kotlinx.coroutines.cancel

  13: import okhttp3.CookieJar
  14: import okhttp3.MediaType.Companion.toMediaTypeOrNull
  15: import okhttp3.OkHttpClient
  16: import okhttp3.Request
  17: import okhttp3.RequestBody.Companion.toRequestBody
  18: import org.json.JSONObject
  19: 
  20: /**
  21:  * Minimal native bridge for inbox-rendered cards. Exposed to the WebView as
  22:  * `window.__syncler_native__`; the shell HTML wraps it in a `window.platform`
  23:  * proxy that mirrors the SDK contract.
  24:  *
  25:  * Only `platform.network.fetch` is wired ג€” the lottery dogfood's "Played"
  26:  * button needs it, and that's the only capability V1 senders rely on. Other
  27:  * methods (storage, camera, notifications, ג€¦) explicitly reject so plugins
  28:  * fail loudly instead of silently no-op'ing. Wiring the full bridge is the
  29:  * next chunk, and it should reuse `:feature:plugin-host`'s bridges rather
  30:  * than re-implement them here.
  31:  */
  32: class CardBridge(
  33:     private val webView: WebView,
  34:     private val declaredEndpoints: List<String>,
  35: ) {
  36:     private val scope = CoroutineScope(SupervisorJob() + Dispatchers.IO)
  37:     private val httpClient = OkHttpClient.Builder()
  38:         .cookieJar(CookieJar.NO_COOKIES)
  39:         .connectionSpecs(
  40:             if (BuildConfig.DEBUG) {
  41:                 listOf(ConnectionSpec.MODERN_TLS, ConnectionSpec.CLEARTEXT)
  42:             } else {
  43:                 listOf(ConnectionSpec.MODERN_TLS)
  44:             },
  45:         )
  46:         .build()
  47: 
  48:     @JavascriptInterface
  49:     fun call(method: String, argsJson: String, callbackId: String) {
  50:         scope.launch {
  51:             val result = runCatching { dispatch(method, argsJson) }
  52:             val payload = if (result.isSuccess) {
  53:                 """{"success":true,"value":${result.getOrThrow()}}"""
  54:             } else {
  55:                 val message = result.exceptionOrNull()?.message ?: "card bridge error"
  56:                 """{"success":false,"error":"call_failed","message":${JSONObject.quote(message)}}"""
  57:             }
  58:             webView.post {
  59:                 webView.evaluateJavascript(
  60:                     "window.__syncler_internal_callback(${JSONObject.quote(callbackId)}, $payload)",
  61:                     null,
  62:                 )
  63:             }
  64:         }
  65:     }
  66: 
  67:     fun destroy() {
  68:         scope.cancel()
  69:     }
  70: 
  71:     private suspend fun dispatch(method: String, argsJson: String): String = when (method) {
  72:         "platform.network.fetch" -> doFetch(argsJson)
  73:         else -> throw UnsupportedOperationException("$method is not wired in inbox mode")
  74:     }
  75: 
  76:     private suspend fun doFetch(argsJson: String): String = withContext(Dispatchers.IO) {
  77:         val args = JSONObject(argsJson)
  78:         val url = args.optString("url").ifBlank { throw IllegalArgumentException("missing url") }
  79:         // Scheme check (defense in depth ג€” the OkHttp client already refuses
  80:         // cleartext in release via its connectionSpecs, but failing explicitly
  81:         // here gives a clearer error and survives future client wiring drift).
  82:         val schemeOk = url.startsWith("https://") || (BuildConfig.DEBUG && url.startsWith("http://"))
  83:         if (!schemeOk) throw SecurityException("fetch URL must be HTTPS: $url")
  84:         if (!matchesAny(url, declaredEndpoints)) {
  85:             throw SecurityException("endpoint not declared: $url")
  86:         }
  87:         val init = args.optJSONObject("init")
  88:         val method = init?.optString("method")?.uppercase()?.takeIf { it.isNotBlank() } ?: "GET"
  89:         val bodyText = init?.optString("body")?.takeIf { it.isNotBlank() && method !in setOf("GET", "HEAD") }
  90:         val mediaType = init?.optString("contentType")?.takeIf { it.isNotBlank() }?.toMediaTypeOrNull()
  91:         val request = Request.Builder().url(url).method(method, bodyText?.toRequestBody(mediaType)).apply {
  92:             init?.optJSONObject("headers")?.let { headers ->
  93:                 headers.keys().forEach { key -> header(key, headers.optString(key)) }
  94:             }
  95:         }.build()
  96: 
  97:         httpClient.newCall(request).execute().use { response ->
  98:             val responseBody = response.body?.string().orEmpty()
  99:             val headersJson = JSONObject().also { h ->
 100:                 response.headers.names().forEach { name ->
 101:                     h.put(name, response.headers(name).joinToString(","))
 102:                 }
 103:             }
 104:             JSONObject()
 105:                 .put("status", response.code)
 106:                 .put("headers", headersJson)
 107:                 .put("body", responseBody)
 108:                 .toString()
 109:         }
 110:     }
 111: 
 112:     private fun matchesAny(url: String, patterns: List<String>): Boolean =
 113:         patterns.any { pattern -> endpointPatternToRegex(pattern).matches(url) }
 114: 
 115:     // Same logic as :feature:plugin-host's EndpointMatcher; inlined here so
 116:     // :feature:inbox doesn't need to depend on the whole plugin-host module
 117:     // graph just for this glob match.
 118:     private fun endpointPatternToRegex(pattern: String): Regex {
 119:         val pathStart = findPathStart(pattern)
 120:         val source = buildString {
 121:             pattern.forEachIndexed { index, character ->
 122:                 if (character == '*') {
 123:                     append(if (index < pathStart) "[^./]*" else "[^/]*")
 124:                 } else {
 125:                     append(Regex.escape(character.toString()))
 126:                 }
 127:             }
 128:         }
 129:         return Regex("^$source$")
 130:     }
 131: 
 132:     private fun findPathStart(pattern: String): Int {
 133:         val schemeEnd = pattern.indexOf("://")
 134:         val searchFrom = if (schemeEnd == -1) 0 else schemeEnd + 3
 135:         val slash = pattern.indexOf('/', searchFrom)
 136:         return if (slash == -1) pattern.length else slash
 137:     }
 138: 
 139:     companion object {
 140:         const val NATIVE_BRIDGE_NAME = "__syncler_native__"
 141:     }
 142: }

   1: package app.syncler.core.crypto
   2: 
   3: import android.os.Build
   4: import android.security.keystore.KeyGenParameterSpec
   5: import android.security.keystore.KeyProperties
   6: import java.security.KeyPairGenerator
   7: import java.security.KeyStore
   8: import java.security.PrivateKey
   9: import java.security.Signature
  10: import org.bouncycastle.asn1.x509.SubjectPublicKeyInfo
  11: import org.bouncycastle.crypto.params.Ed25519PrivateKeyParameters
  12: import org.bouncycastle.crypto.params.Ed25519PublicKeyParameters
  13: import org.bouncycastle.crypto.signers.Ed25519Signer
  14: 
  15: object Signing {
  16:     const val DEVICE_KEY_ALIAS = "syncler-device-ed25519-v1"
  17: 
  18:     fun publicKeyFromSeed(seed: ByteArray): ByteArray {
  19:         require(seed.size == KEY_SIZE_BYTES)
  20:         return Ed25519PrivateKeyParameters(seed, 0).generatePublicKey().encoded
  21:     }
  22: 
  23:     fun signWithSeed(seed: ByteArray, message: ByteArray): ByteArray {
  24:         require(seed.size == KEY_SIZE_BYTES)
  25:         val signer = Ed25519Signer()
  26:         signer.init(true, Ed25519PrivateKeyParameters(seed, 0))
  27:         signer.update(message, 0, message.size)
  28:         return signer.generateSignature()
  29:     }
  30: 
  31:     fun verify(publicKey: ByteArray, message: ByteArray, signature: ByteArray): Boolean {
  32:         if (publicKey.size != KEY_SIZE_BYTES || signature.size != 64) return false
  33:         val verifier = Ed25519Signer()
  34:         verifier.init(false, Ed25519PublicKeyParameters(publicKey, 0))
  35:         verifier.update(message, 0, message.size)
  36:         return verifier.verifySignature(signature)
  37:     }
  38: 
  39:     fun androidKeystorePublicKeyOrNull(alias: String = DEVICE_KEY_ALIAS): ByteArray? {
  40:         if (Build.VERSION.SDK_INT < Build.VERSION_CODES.S) return null
  41:         return runCatching {
  42:             val keyStore = KeyStore.getInstance("AndroidKeyStore").apply { load(null) }
  43:             if (keyStore.containsAlias(alias)) {
  44:                 val raw = SubjectPublicKeyInfo
  45:                     .getInstance(keyStore.getCertificate(alias).publicKey.encoded)
  46:                     .publicKeyData.bytes
  47:                 if (raw.size == KEY_SIZE_BYTES) return@runCatching raw
  48:                 // Stale alias from a previous build that stored a non-Ed25519 key
  49:                 // (e.g. Samsung Keystore silently substituted P-256). Drop it so
  50:                 // the next generation attempt ג€” or the BC fallback ג€” produces a
  51:                 // valid 32-byte Ed25519 key.
  52:                 keyStore.deleteEntry(alias)
  53:             }
  54:             val generator = KeyPairGenerator.getInstance("Ed25519", "AndroidKeyStore")
  55:             generator.initialize(
  56:                 KeyGenParameterSpec.Builder(
  57:                     alias,
  58:                     KeyProperties.PURPOSE_SIGN or KeyProperties.PURPOSE_VERIFY,
  59:                 ).build(),
  60:             )

   1: # Syncler examples
   2: 
   3: Two reference examples, one per layer:
   4: 
   5: - [`trading-bot/`](trading-bot/) ג€” **sender side**. A Python backend using `sdk-python` to register, pair, and push messages to a user's phone every 30 minutes. Doesn't ship a plugin; pair it with the minimal plugin below for a full round-trip.
   6: - [`../sdk-plugin/examples/minimal/`](../sdk-plugin/examples/minimal/) ג€” **plugin side**. The smallest WebView script-renderer plugin: one `BasePlugin` subclass, one `render()` returning HTML, the `registerPlugin(...)` call. Source + build script + unsigned manifest. Run the sign-bundle tool to populate `bundleHash` and `signature` before publishing.
   7: 
   8: A full round-trip example (`trading-bot` sender wired to a `trading-bot` plugin, both sharing a `state.json`) is tracked on the V1.5 DX roadmap.
   9:

 succeeded in 301ms:
   1: # minimal
   2: 
   3: Reference WebView (script-renderer) plugin. The smallest possible end-to-end shape ג€” a `BasePlugin` subclass with a `render()` that returns HTML, plus the `registerPlugin(...)` call the host expects.
   4: 
   5: ## Files
   6: 
   7: - `src/plugin.ts` ג€” the plugin source (one class, one render).
   8: - `manifest.json` ג€” the **unsigned** manifest. The `bundleHash` and `signature` fields are placeholders; `tools/sign-bundle.ts` fills them in.
   9: - `build.sh` ג€” esbuild invocation that produces `dist/plugin.bundle.js`.
  10: - `dist/` ג€” build output (gitignored if your global ignore covers `dist/`; tracked here so the example round-trips even without `npm install`).
  11: 
  12: ## Build ג†’ sign ג†’ publish
  13: 
  14: ```sh
  15: # 1. Build the IIFE bundle (NOT ESM ג€” the host loads it in a <script> tag).
  16: ./build.sh
  17: 
  18: # 2. Sign it. The signer reads manifest.json (placeholders), computes
  19: #    SHA-256 over the bundle bytes, signs `(canonical manifest || bundleHash)`
  20: #    with your Ed25519 sender key, writes manifest.signed.json with the
  21: #    real bundleHash and signature.
  22: npx tsx ../../tools/sign-bundle.ts \
  23:   dist/plugin.bundle.js \
  24:   ~/.syncler/keys/sender.pem \
  25:   manifest.json \
  26:   manifest.signed.json
  27: 
  28: # 3. Publish via the Python SDK (your backend, one time per version).
  29: #    See ../../README.md and docs/integration-guide.md ֲ§5.
  30: ```
  31: 
  32: ## What this example does NOT do (yet)
  33: 
  34: This is a script-renderer example with no backend round-trip. A full plugin + backend pair is on the V1.5 DX track (see `docs/ROADMAP.md`). For a sender-side example, look at `../../../examples/trading-bot/`.
  35: 
  36: ## Why the placeholders look weird
  37: 
  38: `bundleHash: 'UNSIGNED-PLACEHOLDER-REPLACE-WITH-SIGN-BUNDLE'` (and the same for `signature`) is deliberate: the SDK's `validatePluginManifest` rejects this as-written (requires 64-hex `bundleHash` + 128-hex `signature`). That's by design ג€” an unsigned manifest can't be published. The placeholder is loud rather than `'00'` so the failure mode is obvious if you forget step 2.

 succeeded in 317ms:
  22: 
  23: ## Minimal Plugin
  24: 
  25: A runnable reference plugin lives at `examples/minimal/`. Source, build script, and unsigned manifest are all there ג€” the README's snippet is the same code in shorter form:
  26: 
  27: ```ts
  28: import { BasePlugin, DismissBehavior, registerPlugin } from '@syncler/plugin-sdk';
  29: 
  30: export class MinimalPlugin extends BasePlugin {
  31:   static manifest = {
  32:     id: 'com.example.minimal',
  33:     name: 'Minimal',
  34:     version: '1.0.0',
  35:     senderId: 'com.example.sender',
  36:     // Placeholders until you run sign-bundle.ts (see ֲ§"Signing" below).
  37:     // The SDK validator REJECTS these ג€” that's the point: an unsigned
  38:     // manifest cannot be published. Build the bundle, then run the
  39:     // signer, which rewrites this file with the real 64-hex bundleHash
  40:     // and 128-hex Ed25519 signature.
  41:     bundleHash: 'UNSIGNED-PLACEHOLDER-REPLACE-WITH-SIGN-BUNDLE',
  42:     signature: 'UNSIGNED-PLACEHOLDER-REPLACE-WITH-SIGN-BUNDLE',
  43:     declaredCapabilities: [],
  44:     declaredEndpoints: [],
  45:     dismissBehavior: DismissBehavior.DISMISS_LOCAL_ONLY,
  46:     minPlatformVersion: '1.0.0',
  47:   };
  48: 
  49:   render(data: { text: string }) {
  50:     return `<div>${data.text}</div>`;
  51:   }
  52: }
  53: 
  54: registerPlugin(new MinimalPlugin());
  55: ```
  56: 
  57: Build the example bundle, then sign it, then validate:
  58: 
  59: ```sh
  60: npm run build:example                                             # writes examples/minimal/dist/plugin.bundle.js
  61: npx tsx tools/sign-bundle.ts \
  62:   examples/minimal/dist/plugin.bundle.js \
  63:   ~/.syncler/keys/sender.pem \
  64:   examples/minimal/manifest.json \
  65:   examples/minimal/manifest.signed.json
  66: ```
  67: 
  68: The signer reads the unsigned `manifest.json`, computes SHA-256 over the bundle, signs `(canonical manifest || bundleHash)` with Ed25519, and writes `manifest.signed.json` with `bundleHash` + `signature` populated. That signed manifest is what passes `validatePluginManifest` and what your backend ships to `client.publish_plugin(...)`.
  69: 
  70: The native host calls `__syncler_internal_dispatch(hook, args)` after loading the plugin bundle. Plugin bundles should register exactly one plugin instance with `registerPlugin`.

 succeeded in 295ms:
  18: ## V1.5 ג€” Plugin runtime + key hygiene
  19: 
  20: 1. **Multi-process plugin host.** Move JS plugin execution to a dedicated Android process via AIDL/Binder. Isolates a crashing or runaway plugin from the host UI process and gives us a clean ProcessRecord boundary for the OS to kill independently.
  21: 2. **Native Kotlin plugin runtime (out-of-process).** A second plugin format alongside the JS bundle: a signed AAR loaded into the isolated process. Performance + platform-API parity for plugin authors who want a native experience, with the IPC boundary preventing in-process ClassLoader poisoning.
  22: 3. **Master-key rotation.** UX + protocol for rotating the user's 32-byte master key without losing access to historical state. Required before per-device encryption (#4) lands.
  23: 4. **Per-device envelope encryption.** Senders encrypt the payload separately for each of the user's enrolled devices, keyed by per-device public keys instead of the shared user master key. Enables forward secrecy and immediate per-device revocation without rotating user-wide keys.
  24: 5. **Durable nonce-replay protection.** Move the per-sender nonce registry from in-memory to Postgres so a worker restart can't accept a replayed envelope.
  25: 
  26: ## V1.5 ג€” Developer experience
  27: 
  28: DX track surfaced by external plugin-author review (lottery-claude, consultation 68). Phase 4.1 closed the small doc/validator wins; this section tracks the larger items that need design or app-side UX work.
  29: 
  30: 6. **Automated pairing handshake.** Today the user reads `user_id` + `pairing_key_hex` off the device confirmation screen and types them into the sender's backend. V1.5 wires the bootstrap exchange end-to-end: the device POSTs the `(user_id, pairing_key)` tuple to a sender-supplied broker URL embedded in the QR; the sender's backend polls a `did the user complete this token?` endpoint and unlocks `set_pairing` automatically. Removes the largest first-impressions papercut. See `sdk-python/README.md` Quickstart for the V1 dogfood flow this replaces.
  31: 7. **Full round-trip example plugin.** `sdk-plugin/examples/minimal/` exists today but only exercises the plugin side; `examples/trading-bot/` exists but only exercises the sender side. V1.5 ships a `trading-bot` example with **both** a plugin and a backend in the same directory, sharing a `state.json`, ready to `./build.sh && python bot.py loop` and produce a real card on a paired device. Sets the floor for what plugin authors expect to copy.
  32: 8. **`npm create @syncler/plugin` scaffold.** Generator that produces a starter plugin (manifest, `src/plugin.ts` with sensible defaults, `build.sh`, `manifest.signed.json` placeholder, an example sender) so new authors aren't reading the integration guide line-by-line. Builds on #7.
  33: 9. **Validator polish backlog.** Centralize "things the SDK validator should reject that we currently let through to the server's 422." Examples: cross-renderer field conflicts already caught (`renderer: 'script'` + `template`), but not yet caught ג€” `card_key` not matching `card_key_path`, illegal characters in plugin `id`, malformed semver components. Each addition reduces the server-side surface area and shortens the iteration loop for new authors.
  34: 
  35: ## V2 ג€” Capability surface
  36: 
  37: 10. **Plugin capability expansion.** Add `camera`, `storage`, `file`, `location`, `gallery` to the bridge with per-grant prompts. Each capability lands with its own audit-log + user-visible permission dialog.
  38: 11. **`message.respond` + `showNotification`.** Promote action callbacks from a fire-and-forget POST to a request/response handshake the plugin can await. Add a `showNotification` bridge so non-inbox-mode flows (background alerts) work.
  39: 12. **Template renderer layouts.** Expand beyond `standard_card` to `compact_row`, `score_card`, and a handful of other layouts driven by data-class types. Each new layout ships with golden render tests.
  40: 13. **Script-fast runtime (Javy/QuickJS).** A lighter, non-WebView execution mode for purely logic-heavy plugins that don't need DOM. Faster cold-start and less memory than the current WebView path.
  41: 
  42: ## V3 ג€” Two-way + scaling
  43: 
  44: 14. **WebSocket two-way channel.** Bidirectional, low-latency channel between plugins and their backends; covers chat, live cursors, presence. Complements but does not replace the SSE hint channel for V1's pull-then-render model.
  45: 15. **`platform.live.subscribe(...)` for script plugins.** API for a script bundle to subscribe to a named feed and receive incremental updates without polling.
  46: 16. **Field-level live subscriptions on templates.** Update specific template fields without re-rendering the whole card ג€” the live-card path today is whole-card upsert; this adds a finer grain.
  47: 17. **Redis pub/sub for SSE scaling.** Move the in-process event bus to a shared backplane so the SSE fanout works across multiple FastAPI workers and pods.
  48: 
  49: ## V4 ג€” UX polish
  50: 
  51: 18. **Guided lost-device rotation flow.** Click-through UX for: revoke lost device ג†’ re-pair on trusted devices ג†’ rotate master key (depends on V1.5 #3). Today the user does steps 1ג€“2 by hand; this automates the sequence.
  52: 19. **Per-plugin user preferences.** Notification cadence, label overrides, delivery-window scheduling, do-not-disturb integration ג€” all surfaced from the host's settings sheet without plugin-side code.

 succeeded in 309ms:
 180: ### 3.1 `declaredEndpoints` glob syntax
 181: 
 182: `declaredEndpoints` controls which URLs your plugin may pass to `platform.network.fetch`. The host (both Android `EndpointMatcher.kt` and the TS SDK's `network.ts`) implements the same glob grammar:
 183: 
 184: - A literal `*` matches **exactly one segment**, never multiple. The boundary changes by position:
 185:   - In the host portion of the URL (before the first `/` after the scheme), `*` matches `[^./]*` ג€” a single host label. `https://*.example.com/feed` matches `https://api.example.com/feed`, but **not** `https://a.b.example.com/feed`.
 186:   - In the path portion, `*` matches `[^/]*` ג€” a single path segment. `https://example.com/api/*` matches `https://example.com/api/v1`, but **not** `https://example.com/api/v1/users`.
 187: - There is no `**` for "any number of segments." You need one entry per depth, or you need to make the path component a single segment (e.g. encode trailing path in a query string).
 188: - Match is anchored: the full URL must match, including query string. To allow a query, include `*` in the path or query position.
 189: 
 190: Example: to allow both `/api/v1/ack` and `/api/v2/ack`, declare both: `["https://example.com/api/v1/*", "https://example.com/api/v2/*"]`. Or, if you don't care about path depth, declare `["https://example.com/api/*", "https://example.com/api/*/*"]` and so on.
 191: 
 192: This is the single most common manifest mistake ג€” a plugin author declares `https://example.com/api/*` and then `fetch`-es `https://example.com/api/v1/users`, which gets rejected with `endpoint_not_declared`. The same pattern controls **template action endpoints** (the publish-time validator uses the same matcher to verify `action.endpoint` is in `endpoints`).
 193: 
 194: ### 3.2 `platform.network.fetch` contract
 195: 
 196: The host bridge wraps a stock OkHttp client. Behavior:
 197: 
 198: - **Returns a `Response`** for any HTTP response (2xx, 4xx, 5xx all resolve). The status is on `response.status`. You're responsible for checking it.
 199: - **Throws** on:
 200:   - `endpoint_not_declared` ג€” URL doesn't match any `declaredEndpoints` glob (see ֲ§3.1).
 201:   - `cleartext_in_release` ג€” `http://` URL in a release build. Debug builds allow cleartext for LAN dev.
 202:   - Network failures (DNS, connection refused, timeout) propagate as an `Error` whose message includes the underlying cause; treat them like a generic offline state.
 203: - **Timeouts**: OkHttp library defaults (no explicit override). That's ~10s connect / 10s read each. If your endpoint can be slow, factor that into your UX (the user is staring at the card).
 204: - **Request shape**: standard `RequestInit` subset. `method`, `headers`, `body` (string), `contentType` are forwarded. No streaming bodies, no `AbortController` in V1.
 205: - **Cookies are disabled** at the bridge (`CookieJar.NO_COOKIES`). Authenticate via headers or signed bodies.
 206: 
 545: 
 546: - **`401 invalid envelope signature`** ג€” your sender's Ed25519 key doesn't match the one registered. Re-check `private_key_path`.
 547: - **`410 plugin missing, revoked, or not owned by sender`** ג€” `plugin_id` (the row UUID) is wrong, or you accidentally used `plugin_identifier`. The two are distinct (see ֲ§5 vs ֲ§6).
 548: - **`410 recipient has no active devices`** ג€” the user has no enrolled device (signed up but never opened the app, or revoked all devices). FCM availability is *not* required; messages are stored regardless and pulled via `/v1/messages/inbox`.
 549: - **`409 nonce already used`** ג€” your code reused a nonce somehow; SDK generates fresh nonces per `send_to`, so this means you're calling `send_to` with cached envelope bytes. Rebuild.
 550: - **`429 rate limited`** ג€” back off + retry per `Retry-After` header.
 551: - **`410 plugin missing, revoked, not live-type, or not owned by sender`** (cards upsert) ג€” the plugin row's `card_type` isn't `"live"`, or the row has a non-null `revoked_at`, or the publish row's `sender_id` doesn't match the signed envelope's sender. The error message is intentionally generic so a probing caller can't distinguish the cases (don't leak which plugin UUIDs exist).
 552: - **`410 no active pairing`** (cards upsert) ג€” the recipient user has not paired with your sender, or the pairing has been revoked. The user needs to re-scan your pairing QR.
 553: - **`400 expires_at exceeds the 48h live-card cap`** (cards upsert) ג€” your supplied `expires_at` is more than 48 hours from now. Live cards are capped server-side to prevent slot squatting. Send shorter and re-upsert to extend.
 554: - **`400 expires_at is not in the future`** (cards upsert) ג€” you sent an already-expired `expires_at`. Use a future timestamp.
 555: - **`409 sequence_number not greater than existing`** (cards upsert) ג€” the existing card has a `sequence_number` ג‰¥ what you sent. Sequence must be strictly increasing per `card_key`.
 556: - **`HostPreviewValidationError: hostPreview.X is N UTF-8 bytes; max is M`** ג€” caught at `client.send_to` time. Trim the offending field; see ֲ§2 for the caps. UTF-8 byte counts, not characters ג€” emoji and accented characters cost more than one byte.
 557: - **`422 manifest validation failed`** (cards/plugins publish) ג€” Pydantic rejected the manifest body. The detail field tells you which check failed. Most common: `template required when renderer == 'template'`, `card_key_path required when card_type == 'live'`, `action endpoint not allowed by declared endpoints`. Mirror this validation client-side via `validatePluginManifest` (TS SDK) to catch before the round-trip.
 558: 
 559: Cross-reference `docs/crypto-spec.md` for the AAD + envelope canonical byte shapes if signatures disagree.
 560: 
 561: ## 9.1 Common pitfalls
 562: 
 563: These pass server-side validation but bite you at runtime. The SDK validator catches most of them now; check here first when something compiles and publishes but doesn't behave.
 564: 
 565: - **`UNSIGNED-PLACEHOLDER-REPLACE-WITH-SIGN-BUNDLE` in `bundleHash` / `signature`.** You forgot to run `sign-bundle.ts` on the built bundle. The SDK validator rejects this (post Phase 4.1) ג€” `bundleHash` must be exactly 64 lowercase hex chars (SHA-256), `signature` must be exactly 128 hex chars (Ed25519). If the SDK lets it through, the server rejects at publish with 422; if both let it through, the device fails the manifest-hash check and shows "Plugin not loaded."
 566: - **`registerPlugin()` not called.** Card shows *"render failed: plugin did not install __syncler_internal_dispatch ג€” missing registerPlugin() call?"*. Your bundle defined the plugin class but never called `registerPlugin(new YourPlugin())` at module scope. The host's bundle loader looks for the dispatcher hook the SDK installs from `registerPlugin`; without it, there's nothing to dispatch into.
 567: - **Single-segment wildcard surprise in `declaredEndpoints`.** `https://example.com/api/*` matches `https://example.com/api/v1` but NOT `https://example.com/api/v1/users`. `*` is one segment, never multiple. Card shows *"endpoint not declared"*. See ֲ§3.1 for the full glob grammar.
 568: - **`card_key` doesn't match `card_key_path` resolved on the plaintext.** The manifest declares `card_key_path: "$.order_id"`; the device extracts that on decrypt and uses it as the merge key. You pass `card_key="order-456"` to `upsert_card`. If the plaintext's `$.order_id` doesn't equal `"order-456"`, the device treats each upsert as a separate row ג€” your "live" card behaves like an event card. The server doesn't cross-check; it's your responsibility.
 569: - **Template/script field mismatches.** Setting `template: {...}` on a `renderer: "script"` manifest, or omitting `template` on `renderer: "template"`. SDK validator catches both. Same with `cardType: "live"` requiring `cardKeyPath` and `cardType: "event"` rejecting it. If the SDK validator misses a case you hit, file a Phase 4.5 doc-bug.
 570: - **Row shows "New message from {sender}" with fallback text only.** Your message was sent without a `hostPreview` block, or the block was malformed (logged + ignored on the device). The detail view still loads the plugin and renders normally; only the row is generic. Add a valid `hostPreview` and re-send.
 571: - **Action POST body shape surprise.** Script renderer: your `onclick` builds whatever body you want. Template renderer: the host POSTs the **entire decrypted payload** verbatim, with no Authorization header. If your endpoint expects `{item_id, acted_at}` and you swapped to template renderer, the endpoint now sees the full payload ג€” adjust the receiver, don't fight the host.
 572: 
 573: ## 10. Versioning + history
 574: 
 575: Publish every plugin release as a new row under the same `plugin_identifier`. `plugin_identifier` is the stable name, while `plugin_row_id` is the exact version row returned by `client.publish_plugin(...)`.

   [sdk-plugin/README.md](D:/Projects/syncler/sdk-plugin/README.md:39) says the signer “rewrites this file,” and [sdk-plugin/examples/minimal/src/plugin.ts](D:/Projects/syncler/sdk-plugin/examples/minimal/src/plugin.ts:15) says `sign-bundle.ts` rewrites `manifest.json`. Server/Android tolerate uppercase, and `sign-bundle.ts` emits lowercase, so this is not a correctness blocker. Either make the regex lowercase-only or change the wording to “64 hex chars.”

One nuance: bridge timeout is explicitly 30s at [PluginBridge.kt](D:/Projects/syncler/android/feature/plugin-host/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/android/pluginhost/PluginBridge.kt:39), so “OkHttp defaults” is true for the client itself, but calls can still be capped by the bridge.

**Validator Strictness**

No false-positive risk for the intended signed manifest path. `sign-bundle.ts` computes SHA-256 hex at [sign-bundle.ts](D:/Projects/syncler/sdk-plugin/tools/sign-bundle.ts:36) and Ed25519 signature hex at line 47. Server publish stores bytes via base64 fields, with exact 32-byte bundle hash and 64-byte signature checks at [schemas.py](D:/Projects/syncler/server/app/schemas.py:535) and [schemas.py](D:/Projects/syncler/server/app/schemas.py:541). Android manifest verification decodes hex and Ed25519 requires 64 bytes at [PluginSignatureVerifier.kt](D:/Projects/syncler/android/feature/plugin-host/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/android/pluginhost/PluginSignatureVerifier.kt:15) and [Signing.kt](D:/Projects/syncler/android/core/crypto/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/core/crypto/Signing.kt:31).

**Overall**

Hold for the two small wording fixes above. The substantive Phase 4.1 fixes are in place; I do not see a functional blocker in the validator, placeholder choice, wildcard docs, fetch contract, or roadmap renumbering.
